Summary 163:
Statistics on the carriage of goods by road by means of vehicles registered in the EU (Regulation (EU) 2018/852)
Statistics on goods by roads by vehicles registered within the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation(EU) No 852/2018 on the collection and transmission of statistical data on the scale and development of the carriage by road of goods and on the degree of utilisation of vehicles carrying out this transport
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to provide the European Commission with comparable, reliable, synchronised, regular and comprehensive statistical data to enable it to monitor and analyse the transport of goods across the EU.
It repeals Regulation (EC) No 223/2009 on European statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
goods road transport vehicles whose authorised weight or dimensions exceed the limits normally permitted in the Member States concerned;
agricultural vehicles, military vehicles and vehicles belonging to central or local public administrations;
vehicles belonging to public undertakings, and in particular railway undertakings.
EU countries must ensure that their methods for collecting and processing the data are designed to ensure that the statistical results transmitted pursuant to this regulation are sufficiently precise so as to enable the Commission to have at its disposal comparable, accurate, reliable and synchronised statistical data, whilst taking account of the structural characteristics of road transport in the European Union (EU).
The data must be collected in each EU country under the authority of the bodies and institutions in charge of compiling official statistics. They must be sent to Eurostat, the Commission’s statistical office, which is responsible for compiling the data.
The Commission has the power to adopt implementing acts for transmitting the data, including, where appropriate, the statistical tables based on those data. The Commission must draw up a report in respect of the delegation of power not later than 9 months before the end of the 5-year period.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 July 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
Road transport statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Carriage by road: the transport by road in which is carried out by a vehicle registered in an EU country.
* Load capacity: the maximum weight of goods declared permissible by the competent authorities of the EU country of registration of the vehicle.
ACT
Commission Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 802/2018 of 12 July 2018 on the harmonisation of the collection, transmission and processing of statistical results on the quantity and type of goods transported by road (recast) (OJ L 183, 14.7.2018, pp. 1-8)
last update 14.07.2019



Summary 164:
Transmission of judicial and extrajudicial documents in civil and commercial matters
Transmission in the Member States of the European Union
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on the service in the EU of judicial or extrajudicial and commercial documents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the transposition of documents between the EU countries for the purpose of serving judicial or commercial matters in another EU country.
KEY POINTS
Each EU country must designate a central body responsible for:
supplying information to the transmitting agencies;
seeking solutions to any difficulties which may arise during transmission of documents for service;
forwarding, in exceptional cases, at the request of a transmitting agency, a request for service to the competent receiving agency.
The transmitting agency must inform the addressee in writing using the standard form that he may refuse to accept the document to be served at the time of service or by returning it to the receiving agency within one week if it is not either in a language which he understands or in the official language or one of the official languages of the place of service.
If it has not been possible to effect service within one month of receipt, the transmitting agency shall:
immediately inform the transmitting agent by means of the standard forms set out in Annex I, which shall be drawn up under the conditions referred to in Article 10(2);
continue to take all necessary steps to effect the service of the document, unless indicated otherwise by the transmitting Agency;
take all necessary measures to ensure that service seems to be possible within a reasonable period of time.
In exceptional cases the applicant may refuse service if the document is not in one of those languages provided for in Article 8. The applicant must be advised by the agency to which he forwards the document for transmission that the person to whom the document has been sent may refuse it if it does not exist in the language of his/her official or official place of residence.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The regulation entered into force on 1 January 2005. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
   
The European Union (EU) has adopted a number of measures to improve the functioning of the internal market, including the establishment of a European Judicial Network in Civil and Commercial Matters.
For more information, see:
‘Judicial cooperation’ on the European Commission’s website.

EU rules on advanced therapy medicinal products for the treatment of diseases and dysfunctions of the human body (Regulation (EU) 2018/852)
EU rules governing advanced therapy medicines for the use of human cells and tissues (Regulations (EU, Euratom and Euratom)
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EC) No 852/2006 on the regulation of advanced therapy therapeutic products for human use
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the manufacture, importation and sale of advanced therapies for the purpose of treating human diseases and disorders.
It aims to ensure that these products comply with the EU’s rules on quality and safety.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all advanced therapy products for use in the EU. It does not apply to gene therapy medicines, somatic cell therapies or stem cell therapies.
Scope of the regulation
It applies to:
tissue engineered products* (e.g. cells or tissues of human or animal origin, or both);
genetic therapies* (i.e. stem cells, stem cells or stem cells derived from human cells)
sensory therapies*;
immuno-oncology* (the use of stem cells and stem cells to treat cancer);
therapeutic devices* (medical devices designed to stimulate the immune system of the body, such as heart valves, heart valves and heart valves).
It does not affect the EU countries’ national laws on the manufacture and importation of medicinal products.
Authorisation
The European Commission must draw up a draft opinion on the quality, safety and efficacy of each advanced therapy product for final approval by the European Agency for Medicinal Products for Human Use (Euratom). This opinion must be published in the Official Journal of the European Union (JHA) every 3 years.
EU countries must ensure that the draft opinion is published in a language easily understood by the public.
The Commission must publish a report on the implementation of this regulation after experience has been gained, with a particular attention to the different types of advanced therapeutic products authorised.

Summary 166:
Emissions from motor vehicles — type approval and access to vehicle repair and maintenance information (Regulation (EU) 2017/852)
Emissions of motor vehicles— type approval
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EC) No 852/2017 on type approval for motor vehicles and their trailers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the type approval of all motor vehicles in the European Union (EU).
It aims to improve the quality of air in the EU by harmonising the technical requirements for the emission of greenhouse gases (GHGs) and particulate matter (PM) in motor vehicles.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to motor vehicles with a reference mass not exceeding 2,840 kg and which meet the conditions laid down in this regulation and its implementing measures.
Vehicles covered by the regulation are M1, M2, N1 and N2 vehicles, as defined in Annex II to Directive 70/156/EEC (see summary).
Manufacturers must apply for type approval within 3 years of the date of sale or putting into service of the vehicle covered by this regulation.
The type approval procedure is based on the following criteria:
the vehicle meets the requirements for:
in-service conformity,
the durability of pollution control devices,
on-board diagnostic (OBD) systems,
fuel consumption and accessibility of vehicle repair/maintenance information.
EU countries must ensure that:
pollution control devices meet the requirements set out in the regulation;
on board diagnostic systems are compatible with the requirements in Annex I to the regulation and meet the minimum requirements for OBD systems;
the fuel consumption and carbon dioxide emissions of vehicles are met in accordance with the regulation’s annexes;
vehicle type approval procedures are reviewed by the European Commission at least every 4 years.
In addition, EU countries must:
ensure that: all new vehicles with an OBD system are type approved by the manufacturer;
all new vehicles that are sold or put into service by the manufacturers must be type approved within 4 years of their arrival on the market;
instructions for the installation of OBDs are available on the manufacturer's website;
information on the OBD and fuel consumption of vehicles must be provided on the website of the authorised dealer or repairers.
Access to vehicle repairs and maintenance services
The European Commission must establish a system of access to all vehicle repairs, maintenance and repair information for independent operators on the same basis as for authorised dealers.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULATION APPLY?
Directive (EC, Euratom) 2018/722 has applied since 1 July 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
Emission from motor cars (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
  * Emissions: the exhaust gas emissions of carbon monoxide, oxides of nitrogen, and hydrocarbons.
* PM: the particulate mass of fine particulates in the air of a vehicle.
** CO2: the carbon dioxide (CO2) and nitrogen oxide (NO2) emissions of a motor vehicle, including from the tailpipe and evaporative emissions.

Summary 167:
European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) — common procedures for substances authorised to be placed on the European Union (EU) market and for their use in foodstuffs (Regulation (EC) No 1334/2008).
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2017/852 — common procedure for substances on the EU market
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION AND OF THE DECISION?
The regulation establishes a common procedure to authorise substances to be put on the market in the EU.
The decision sets out the procedures to be followed by the EFSA.
KEY POINTS
Scope
This regulation applies to substances that have been authorised by the EU’s sectoral food laws. It does not apply to food additives, food enzymes and food flavourings.
It applies to all substances that can be used in and on foods.
Risk assessment and authorisation procedure
The EFSA carries out an independent risk assessment of substances to determine whether they pose a risk to human health. It then forwards its opinion to the European Commission, the EU countries and, where applicable, the applicant. The opinion is published in the Official Journal of the EU and is binding on all EU countries.
EU countries must notify the EFTA within 14 working days of receiving the application and request its opinion within 3 months of receiving it.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISIONS APPLY?
   
The delegated regulation has applied since 1 July 2017.
BACKGROUND
 
  ‘Food safety’ is a key element of EU policy. It aims to ensure a high level of protection of human life and health in the pursuit of EU policies.
For more information, see:
Food safety (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Authorised substance: a substance which contributes to the free movement of food within the EU, and to a high degree of protection for human health and to the protection of consumer interests.
* Additives: substances which have the ability to enhance the flavour, colour, texture or texture of foods. They may be used as a colouring agent, as a preservative, as an emulsifier or as a flavouring agent.

Summary 169:
EU-Nordic agreement on the extradition of suspects and their families
EU-Norwegian agreement onthe extradition of suspected and their family
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Union (EU) and its Member States, the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland on the cooperation of their judicial authorities in the execution of an arrest warrant
Decision (EU, Euratom) 2017/852 on the conclusion of the agreement between the EU and the Nordic countries on the negotiation of an extradition agreement
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND THE DECISION?
The agreement aims to ensure that the extradition system between EU countries and, on the other hand, the countries of the Nordic area is based on a mechanism of surrender.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The extradition procedure between EU and Nordic countries is governed by a common extradition procedure.
EU countries have uniform extradition laws with a common concept of extradition.
Each EU country has a judicial authority which is competent to issue an extradition warrant.
An arrest warrant is issued by the judicial authority of the country in which the offence was committed. The warrant is valid for a period of 6 months and may be renewed if the offence is committed in another EU country.
A judicial authority may refuse to execute the warrant if it considers that the offence has been committed in the territory of the issuing country or in a place treated as such, or if the act was committed outside the country of issuing country and the law of the executing country does not allow prosecution for the same offences when committed outside its territory.
If the arrest warrant has been issued for the purpose of prosecution or execution of a sentence, the executing judicial authority must inform the EU country which issued the warrant of the reasons for refusing to execute it.
In the event of non-execution of the warrant, EU countries may make a declaration to the other EU countries to the effect that nationals will not be surrendered or that surrender will be authorised only under certain specified conditions.
When an EU country receives a request for the surrender of a non-EU country’s nationals, it must send the request to the national judicial authority in the country where the requested person is resident. The judicial authority is responsible for verifying that the request is genuine and that the person has given his or her consent to be surrendered.
Where the request for surrender is not genuine, the issuing judicial authority has the right to refuse the warrant and to issue a new arrest warrant in the event that the requested persons has not given his/her consent.
FROM WHEN DOES THE AGEMENT AND DECISION APPLY?
Both decisions have applied since 1 January 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Arrest warrant’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Arrest warrant: an international arrest warrant issued by a country in order to arrest a person who is a national of that country and who has been convicted of a criminal offence in that country. It may be issued by any country in the world, including the EU, as long as the person is an EU national.

Summary 170:
Railway ticketing and ticketing — passengers’ rights
Train ticketing & ticketing
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on the carriage of passengers by rail
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to protect the rights of passengers when travelling by rail by rail in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all rail passenger services throughout the EU. It does not apply to:
the carriage of goods by rail;
the sale of tickets by railway undertakings or ticket vendors;
accessibility of trains for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility;
fares and special conditions;
information and service quality requirements.
It repeals Directive 2001/14/EC.
EU countries may grant temporary exemptions from the application of the regulation to certain services or journeys because a significant part of the rail passenger service, including at least one scheduled station stop, is operated outside the EU or is operated by an EU-owned railway company.
Railway undertakings and station managers must:
take into account the needs of passengers and their families;
ensure that all buildings and rolling stock are made accessible to users;
take measures to ensure the personal security of passengers in railway stations and on trains and to manage risk.
Passengers must be able to purchase tickets for travel by rail to do so without undue difficulty;
have access to the information and service they need to make a reservation;
be able to use the ticketing system;
use the information provided by the ticket vendor and the ticket office at the railway station;
make use of the information system provided for in Regulation (TSI);
have the right of refusal to purchase a ticket if they do not meet the conditions set out in the regulation;
notify passengers of any delays or cancellations of a rail service.
Transport contract
A transport contract is a contract of carriage for reward or free of charge between a railway undertaking or a ticket vendor or the passenger for the provision of one or more transport services.
The transport contract must include the following conditions:
transport contract must be concluded and concluded in writing and must be executed in accordance with the rules of the European Commission’s communication ‘Consumer Protection in the field of transport’ (2002-2006)
the transport contract shall be concluded by the railway undertaking in writing or in writing, and shall include the conditions for the conclusion and performance of the transport contract and the terms and conditions for payment of the contract.
Ticketing
The carriage of rail tickets must not be subject to a fare or special conditions. The carriage of railway tickets must be free and without prejudice to the conditions laid down in the Transport Safety Information System (TSIS).
Railways must also:
not charge for the sale of a ticket for a rail ticket;
allow passengers to use a ticket vending machine for the purpose of making a reservation for a train service;
provide a ticketing facility at the station where the ticket is to be purchased;
carry out ticketing without charge at the ticket vending machines at the stations where the tickets are to be sold;
give passengers the right to refuse a ticket on the grounds that they are unable to pay for a ticket or that they have not paid for the ticket.
Exemption from the regulation
An EU country may grant an exemption for a maximum period of 5 years, which may be renewed, from certain provisions which should apply to certain rail passenger journeys because of the operation of the railway passenger service or journeys. The exemption may also be renewed if the exemption is granted for a period of 10 years.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive (EU) 2017/849 amends Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 652/06 to apply the regulation from 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
Rail transport and ticket vending (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
  �   б  х  ̃   Ā 
Commission Regulation (EEC, EC) No 550/2006 of 20 December 2006 on the transport of passengers (OJ L 183, 21.12.2006, pp. 1-18)

Summary 172:
EU energy statistics — reporting and dissemination of energy data (2009-2013)
EU energy data — reporting & dissemination of Energy statistics (2009 - 2013)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on the reporting of energy statistics by EU countries
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that EU countries provide reliable, up-to-date and comparable energy data to the European Commission (Eurostat) and the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries, except Denmark, Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway, Switzerland and the United Kingdom (1).
EU countries must provide data on:
energy production, trade, stocks, transformation, consumption and structural characteristics of the energy system such as installed capacities for electricity generation or production capacities for oil products;
energy consumption;
quality of data;
the quality of data transmitted to Eurostat.
Reporting and dissemination
Each year, EU countries must send Eurostat a report on the quality of the data transmitted as well as on any methodological changes that have been made.
The data must be sent by:
the national statistical authorities of the EU countries;
other sources such as undertakings and other sources specified in the regulation’s annexes;
inform Eurostat of any changes to the transmission arrangements made by the national statistics authorities.
the Commission may grant exemptions or derogations to EU countries from those aspects of the information collection that would lead to an excessive burden on respondents.
Eurostat must ensure that the data collection does not lead to duplication of data collection and that the reporting burden is reasonable.
Each EU country must also provide Eurostat with:
a list of data sources and technical terms used;
a description of the types of data to be transmitted and the technical terms to be used in the reporting;
an annual nuclear statistics report, which must be reported and disseminated from 2009 onwards, that year being the first reported period, without prejudice to confidentiality, where it is necessary, and avoiding any duplication, while at the same time keeping production costs low and reporting burden reasonable. The Commission may, in cooperation with the nuclear energy sector in the EU, define a set of nuclear statistics which shall be reported from 2009 onward.
Every 5 years, Eurostat must provide the Commission with a report, including a list of the national and EU statistical authorities responsible for reporting and disseminating energy data, on the data they have transmitted and on the methodological changes they have made. These reports must be published in the Official Journal.
National statistics must be based on the following categories of data:
production, trade and stocks;
transmission arrangements;
aggregates;
final energy consumption statistics.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?

Summary 173:
Non-discrimination and assistance for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility on the bus and coach — rules for non-discrimination in the transport sector
Non-discriminatory and assistance during the travel sector
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 — rules on the rights of passengers on buses and coaches
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that passengers travelling by bus or coach in the EU have the same level of protection as those of other citizens.
It lays down rules for the rights and assistance of disabled people and persons who have reduced mobility during their journey.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to passengers travelling with occasional services where the initial boarding point or the final alighting point of the passenger is situated in the territory of an EU country.
Passengers must be fully informed of their rights under this regulation, so that they can effectively exercise those rights.
EU countries must ensure that carriers, travel agents and tour operators:
ensure that disabled passengers have access to the carriage of their goods and services;
provide them with information regarding the service before and during the journey;
make available the appropriate assistance to enable them to make use of the carriage;
inform the disabled person or person who has reduced mobility of the reasons therefor, and, upon request, inform the person in question in writing within 5 working days of the request.
Carriers and travel agents must also ensure that:
the carriage of goods is free of charge;
the disabled person is provided with free mobility assistance at the ticketing and boarding and alighting points;
information is made available on the website of the carrier and at the terminal of the travel agent;
travel agents are responsible for managing disabled persons’ mobility;
there is a free mobility service at the travel agents’ premises.
The legislation does not apply to:
passengers travelling on a package tour referred to in Directive 90/314/EEC;
passenger rights in the event of cancellation of a regular service.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
Directive 2009/65/EC on the conditions of carriage of passengers by public transport (see summary) has applied since 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has published a report on the implementation of the regulation since its entry into force on 1 July 2017.
For more information, see:
‘Passenger rights’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Passenger: a person with a disability or reduced mobility who is travelling by road or by rail.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC) No 852/2017 of 20 July 2017 on the rules for bus and coaches (OJ L 183, 21.7.2017, pp. 1-22)
last update 14.01.2019



Summary 174:
Hatching and breeding of fish for aquaculture purposes in EU waters
Hatching & breeding of fishes for aquatic purposes in European waters
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on the production of statistics for the purposes of the monitoring and management of the fisheries sector within the Common Fisheries Policy (CFP)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that EU countries collect accurate and comparable statistics on fish and molluscs produced by hatcheries and nurseries for the purpose of monitoring and managing the EU’s fisheries sector.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries’ fisheries activities conducted in freshwater and saltwater on their territory. It does not apply to:
aquaculture activities conducted on the territory of non-EU countries;
the production of live weight by volume or by number of aquatic organisms;
fisheries conducted in non-fishery waters other than those used by EU countries.
EU countries must use surveys or other statistically validated methods covering at least 90 % of the total production by volume, by number or by weight of the product.
Annexes II, III and IV of the regulation specify the methods to be used to collect the data.
The EU countries must submit the data to the European Commission (Eurostat) within 12 months of the end of the reference calendar year. The first reference year was 2008.
Each EU country must submit a report to Eurostat by 31 December 2011 and every 3 years thereafter on the statistics compiled pursuant to this regulation and on the relevance and quality of the statistics.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRYDATE OF ENTRY AND ENTRY INTO FORCEVIDEOS
   
The legislation entered into force on 1 January 2008. EU countries had to incorporate it into their national statistical systems by 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
Aquaculture plays an important role in the EU fisheries sector and contributes to the EU's total fisheries production.
For more information, see:
Fisheries (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Hatcheries: open or covered enclosed structures constructed with net, mesh or any porous material allowing natural water interchange.
Nurseries: open cages containing live aquatic animals (e.g. fish, crustaceans, crustacesans, mussels, oysters).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU) No 550/2008 of 20 December 2008 on the collection of statistics in the field of fisheries for the means of the management of fisheries within the Community (OJ L 183, 21.12.2008, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 550 / 2008 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS
 
Regulations (EC and EFTA) No 1282/2003 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 December 2003 on the statistical framework for fisheries and repealing Council Regulation No 788/96 of 17 February 1997 on Community Statistics (O J L 284, 31.12.-34.2003)
Commission Regulation (EEC) 2017/852 of 27 February 2017 on the European Union’S fisheries statistics system (OJO) (OJC L 6, 28.2.2017, pp 1-2)

Summary 175:
Control and enforcement of fishing vessels in the North-East Atlantic fisheries — rules and conditions for the EU’s application of the scheme of control and enforcement in the area covered by the Convention on the conservation and management of fishery resources in the north-east Atlantic fisheries (the Convention Area).
ACT
Council Regulation (EU) 2018/852 of 26 February 2018 on the application by the EU of the Scheme of Control and Enforcement in the areas covered by multilateral cooperation on the rational conservation and managed management of fisheries in the region of the Convention Area.
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It lays down the general rules for EU countries’ application by way of the North East Atlantic Fisheries Commission (NEAFC) of the regulation adopted by the European Parliament and of the Council of 15 November 2006 establishing a scheme to control and enforce fishing vessels operating in the waters of the convention area which lie beyond the waters under the fisheries jurisdiction of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to fishing vessels flying the flag of EU countries and operating in waters that lie outside the jurisdiction of NEAFC and which are within the waters governed by the convention.
Vessels flying the EU flag are subject to the same rules as those of the other contracting parties.
EU countries must ensure that vessels flying their flag are inspected at sea and that they carry out inspections in accordance with the rules laid down in the regulation.
The EU countries must:
ensure that vessels carrying out fishing operations are accompanied by an inspector;
carry out inspections at least once a day;
inform the competent authority of the flag EU country of the number of inspectors assigned to carry out the inspection;
keep a logbook of all fishing operations;
send a report to the competent authorities of each flag country within 15 days of the end of the fishing operation;
report on catches on board when entering the regulatory area.
FROM WHEN DO THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
They apply from 26 February 2019.
BACKGROUND
The North-E-Atlantic Fisheries Commission is a multilateral organisation which aims to ensure the conservation, management and sustainable management of the fisheries of the north east Atlantic Ocean.
For more information, see:
Fishery resources (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
Fishing vessel: any fishing vessel flying a flag of an EU country.
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009: the regulation lays down rules for the implementation by EU countries of the European Union (now the European Commission) of a scheme of controls and enforcement for fishing vessels of the Union which are authorised to fish in the regulatory areas of the NEEAFC.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision (EU, Euratom) No 852/2018 of 25 February 2018 laying down general rules and requirements for the application in the Union of the Regulation (EC), the regulation implementing the Convention of the Parties to the Convention in the Area of the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources in the Far North-West Atlantic and repealing Regulation (Euratom, Euratom) (OJ L 347, 26.2.2018, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
Regulations (EC, Euram) No 1082/2008 and (EURAM) No 1182/2009 of the Commission on the implementation of the Regulations of the Member States and the European Atomic Energy Community of the Treaty on the Functioning of the Atomic Energy System (TFEU) and on the European Maritime Safety Agency (EASA) and repealing Regulations (EEC, EEC, EFTA, EASA, EEA, EAFE, EAA, ECA, EAE, ESEA, EEE, EMEA, IEA, IAE, IAA, ICA, IAFE and IAA of the International Maritime Organization (IMO) and the International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC).
Commission Decision (Eureka) No 552/2008 of 26 November 2008 laying down the rules and general principles concerning mechanisms for the control by Member States of their exercise of implementing powers under the regulation and laying down in advance by a regulation adopted in accordance of the ordinary legislative procedure.
Commission Regulation (C) No 624/2008 laying down detailed rules and procedures for the exercise of the implementing powers of the Eureka Regulation and implementing the EEA Regulation.

Summary 176:
Ecolabel — voluntary environmental labelling for food, animal feed and cosmetics (EU Ecolabel)
Ecolabelling – voluntary environmental label for food and animal feed
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 834/2007 — the voluntary EU environmental label
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the establishment and application of the voluntary European Union (EU) ecolabel scheme.
It aims to encourage higher environmental performance in all sectors for which environmental impact is a factor in consumer choice.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to food and feed products, as well as unprocessed agricultural products that lie within the scope of Regulation (EC).
It does not apply to medicinal products for human use, as defined in Directive 2001/83/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 6 November 2001 on the Community code relating to medicines, or for veterinary use, nor to any type of medical device.
The European Union Environment Board (EUEB) evaluates the environmental performance of products and decides on the award of the EU Ecolibel.
Eligibility
Only products certified as organic would be eligible for the award.
Operators must:
have a turnover of at least €500,000 per year;
have an annual turnover of no more than €1.5 million;
notify the European Commission within 6 months of receiving the award;
ensure that the award is valid for at least 6 years;
provide the EU Commission with all the necessary documentation to prove that the product meets the criteria;
check that the products they sell comply with the requirements of the regulation;
make sure that the labelling is clearly visible on the packaging of the products;
keep a record of the number of products they have sold and the information they have provided to the Commission.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The EU EColabel scheme entered into force on 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
‘Environmental labelling’ on the EU’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products protected by patents and certificates in the European Union (EU) and the European Free Trade Association (EFTA) (European Medicines Agency)
Protecting medicinal products covered by a patent and certificates
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on the protection of medicines covered by patents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the holder of a patent* and a certificate* enjoys an overall maximum of 15 years of exclusivity from the time the medicinal product in question first obtains authorisation to be placed on the market in the EU.
KEY POINTS
Protection
The protection conferred by a certificate is limited to the product covered by the basic patent. It does not apply to certificates granted in accordance with their national legislation before 1 January 1995.
The certificate is valid for 15 years from the date on which the patent is granted.
An application for a certificate must be lodged within 6 months of the date of the patent being granted, provided that the application is lodged within six months of:
1 January 2000;
1 July 2002 if the market authorisation was obtained before that date; or
1 May 2004 if the product was obtained after 1 January 2000.
Applications for an extension of the duration of the certificate must contain the particulars referred to in Article 7(3) of the regulation and a copy of a certificate already granted or where an application for an extended duration is pending.
A certificate may be revoked if the patent exceeds 20 years.
Expiry the certificate may lapse at the end of the period provided for in Article 13 if by which the term of the patented patent is longer than 20 years or if the life expectancy of the holder exceeds 70 years. If the certificate lapses or is invalid, notification of the revocation shall be published by the competent national authority responsible under national law for the revocation of the corresponding basic patent in the relevant EU country.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 May 2006 and had to become law in the Member States by 1 May 2007.
BACKGROUND
The European Medicines Authority (EMEA) is responsible for administering the EU’s laws on medicinal products.
For more information, see:
‘Licensing of Medicines’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Patent: a patent granted by an EU country on a medicinal product which is protected by a valid basic patent and for which the first authorisation is granted to place the product on the EU market.
• Certificate: a certificate issued by an authority of the Member State in which the product is protected and valid for a period of at least 15 years after the patent has expired.

Summary 178:
Convention on the jurisdiction of the European Court of Justice in civil and commercial matters in the European Union (EEC) and the European Free Trade Association (EFTA) countries
Council Decision (EU) 2017/852 — conclusion of the Convention on the exclusive jurisdiction of European Court for the protection of the rights of the persons covered by the EEC Convention
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that EU countries’ courts have exclusive jurisdiction in all matters covered by their national laws. It does not apply to revenue, customs or administrative matters.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EEC convention applies to all EU countries, regardless of their nationality. It covers all civil, commercial and criminal matters, including:
contracts, including contracts for the sale of goods on instalment credit terms and loans repayable by instalments, or for any other form of credit, made to finance the purchase of goods;
the protection of personal property, including the right to be sued in the courts of the country in which the contract was entered into;
rights in rem in immovable property, such as a right to live or work in the country where the property is situated;
protection of intellectual property rights such as patents, trademarks, copyrights, trade marks, etc.
jurisdiction of the courts and tribunals.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
The Convention entered into force in the EU countries on 1 January 2018.
Decision (EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Convention for the Protection of the Rights of the Persons Lived in the Community (ECPIC) was signed by the European Community (now the EU) and its Member States on 5 October 1973.
For more information, see:
EEC and EFTA (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
   
Council decision (EU, Euratom) 2017 / 852 of 20 December 2017 on the conclusion, by the Council of the Union, and by the EFTA countries of 1 January 2020, of the Conventions on the Exclusive Jurisdiction in Civil and Commercial Matters (EFC Convention) (OJ L 347, 29.12.2017, pp. 1-8)
Council Directive (EU), Euratom, Euratomic Council and Euratom of 20 January 2020 on the concluding of the EFC Convention of the Community and the conclusion by the EU of the CONVICTS on the Rights and Privileges of the People Lived In The Community and of the Free Trade Associations (COPIC) (Official Journal L 345, 30.1.2020, p. 1)
